</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-below" style="padding-top:0.15em;">
<ul><li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_coloured_voting_box.svg"><img alt="icon" class="noviewer thumbborder" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" decoding="async" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/16px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/24px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/32px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png 2x" width="16"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Politics" title="Portal:Politics">Politics portal</a></li></ul></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1063604349" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Nationalism_sidebar" title="Template:Nationalism sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Nationalism_sidebar" title="Template talk:Nationalism sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Nationalism_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Ultranationalism, combined with the myth of national rebirth, is a key foundation of fascism.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006b451–453"Nationalism"_213-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006b451–453"Nationalism"-213'>[213]</a></sup> Robert Paxton argues that "a passionate nationalism" is the basis of fascism, combined with "a conspiratorial and Manichean view of history" which holds that "the chosen people have been weakened by political parties, social classes, unassimilable minorities, spoiled rentiers, and rationalist thinkers."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPaxton200441_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPaxton200441-214">[214]</a></sup> Roger Griffin identifies the core of fascism as being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palingenetic" title="Palingenetic">palingenetic</a> ultranationalism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGriffin199126_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGriffin199126-41">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>The fascist view of a nation is of a single organic entity that binds people together by their ancestry and is a natural unifying force of people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZimmer200380–107ch._4_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZimmer200380–107ch._4-215">[215]</a></sup> Fascism seeks to solve economic, political and social problems by achieving a <a href="/wiki/Millenarianism" title="Millenarianism">millenarian</a> national rebirth, exalting the nation or <a href="/wiki/Race_(biology)" title="Race (biology)">race</a> above all else and promoting cults of unity, strength and purity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPaxton2004_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPaxton2004-216">[216]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (October 2021)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPassmore2002_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPassmore2002-217">[217]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (October 2021)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGriffin1991_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGriffin1991-218">[218]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (October 2021)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaqueur1997223_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaqueur1997223-219">[219]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEncyclopedia_Britannica_''Fascism''_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEncyclopedia_Britannica_''Fascism''-6">[6]</a></sup> European fascist movements typically espouse a racist conception of non-Europeans being inferior to Europeans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPayne199511_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPayne199511-220">[220]</a></sup> Beyond this, fascists in Europe have not held a unified set of racial views.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPayne199511_220-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPayne199511-220">[220]</a></sup> Historically, most fascists promoted imperialism, although there have been several fascist movements that were uninterested in the pursuit of new imperial ambitions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPayne199511_220-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPayne199511-220">[220]</a></sup> For example, Nazism and Italian Fascism were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Expansionist" title="Expansionist">expansionist</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irredentist" title="Irredentist">irredentist</a>. Falangism in Spain envisioned the worldwide unification of Spanish-speaking peoples (<a href="/wiki/Hispanidad" title="Hispanidad">Hispanidad</a>). <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Fascism" title="British Fascism">British Fascism</a> was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-interventionist" title="Non-interventionist">non-interventionist</a>, though it did embrace the British Empire.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Totalitarianism">Totalitarianism</span></h3>
<p>Fascism promotes the establishment of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Totalitarian" title="Totalitarian">totalitarian</a> state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGriffin20131–6_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGriffin20131–6-12">[12]</a></sup> It opposes liberal democracy, rejects multi-party systems, and may support a <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party state</a> so that it may synthesize with the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMussolini200240_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMussolini200240-13">[13]</a></sup> Mussolini's <i>The Doctrine of Fascism</i> (1932), partly <a href="/wiki/Ghostwriter" title="Ghostwriter">ghostwritten</a> by philosopher <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Gentile" title="Giovanni Gentile">Giovanni Gentile</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELyttelton197313_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELyttelton197313-221">[221]</a></sup> who Mussolini described as "the philosopher of Fascism", states: "The Fascist conception of the State is all-embracing; outside of it no human or spiritual values can exist, much less have value. Thus understood, Fascism is totalitarian, and the Fascist State—a synthesis and a unit inclusive of all values—interprets, develops, and potentiates the whole life of a people."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMussolini193514_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMussolini193514-222">[222]</a></sup> In <i>The Legal Basis of the Total State</i>, Nazi political theorist <a href="/wiki/Carl_Schmitt" title="Carl Schmitt">Carl Schmitt</a> described the Nazi intention to form a "strong state which guarantees a totality of political unity transcending all diversity" in order to avoid a "disastrous pluralism tearing the German people apart."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitt199572_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitt199572-223">[223]</a></sup>
</p><p>Fascist states pursued policies of social <a href="/wiki/Indoctrination" title="Indoctrination">indoctrination</a> through <a href="/wiki/Propaganda" title="Propaganda">propaganda</a> in education and the media, and regulation of the production of educational and media materials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPauley2003117Payne1995220_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPauley2003117Payne1995220-224">[224]</a></sup> Education was designed to glorify the fascist movement and inform students of its historical and political importance to the nation. It attempted to purge ideas that were not consistent with the beliefs of the fascist movement and to teach students to be obedient to the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPauley2003117–119_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPauley2003117–119-225">[225]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economics_of_fascism" title="Economics of fascism">Economics of fascism</a></div>
<p>Fascism presented itself as an alternative to both international <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free-market_capitalism" title="Free-market capitalism">free-market capitalism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBastowMartin200336_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBastowMartin200336-226">[226]</a></sup> While fascism opposed mainstream socialism, fascists sometimes regarded their movement as a type of nationalist "socialism" to highlight their commitment to <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a>, describing it as national <a href="/wiki/Solidarity" title="Solidarity">solidarity</a> and unity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006610_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006610-228">[228]</a></sup> Fascists opposed international free market capitalism, but supported a type of productive capitalism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeld1980_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeld1980-122">[122]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (October 2021)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpektorowskiIreni-Saban2013_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpektorowskiIreni-Saban2013-229">[229]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (November 2021)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Economic self-sufficiency, known as autarky, was a major goal of most fascist governments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Grand199560–61_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Grand199560–61-230">[230]</a></sup>
</p><p>Fascist governments advocated for the resolution of domestic <a href="/wiki/Class_conflict" title="Class conflict">class conflict</a> within a nation in order to guarantee national unity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGriffin1991222–223_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGriffin1991222–223-231">[231]</a></sup> This would be done through the state mediating relations between the classes (contrary to the views of <a href="/wiki/Classical_liberalism" title="Classical liberalism">classical liberal</a>-inspired capitalists).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoover193513–20_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoover193513–20-232">[232]</a></sup> While fascism was opposed to domestic class conflict, it was held that bourgeois-proletarian conflict existed primarily in national conflict between <a href="/wiki/Proletarian_nation" title="Proletarian nation">proletarian nations</a> versus <a href="/wiki/Bourgeois_nation" title="Bourgeois nation">bourgeois nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeocleous199721–22_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeocleous199721–22-233">[233]</a></sup> Fascism condemned what it viewed as widespread character traits that it associated as the typical bourgeois mentality that it opposed, such as: materialism, crassness, cowardice, and the inability to comprehend the heroic ideal of the fascist "warrior"; and associations with liberalism, individualism and parliamentarianism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006102_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006102-234">[234]</a></sup> In 1918, Mussolini defined what he viewed as the proletarian character, defining proletarian as being one and the same with producers, a <a href="/wiki/Productivism" title="Productivism">productivist</a> perspective that associated all people deemed productive, including entrepreneurs, technicians, workers and soldiers as being proletarian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPirainoFiorito200939–41_235-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPirainoFiorito200939–41-235">[235]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (November 2021)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> He acknowledged the historical existence of both bourgeois and proletarian producers but declared the need for bourgeois producers to merge with proletarian producers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPirainoFiorito200939–41_235-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPirainoFiorito200939–41-235">[235]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (November 2021)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VW_Typ_83_vr.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1804" data-file-width="2187" decoding="async" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/VW_Typ_83_vr.jpg/220px-VW_Typ_83_vr.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/VW_Typ_83_vr.jpg/330px-VW_Typ_83_vr.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/VW_Typ_83_vr.jpg/440px-VW_Typ_83_vr.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VW_Typ_83_vr.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The need for a <i>people's car</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a></i> in German), its concept and its functional objectives were formulated by <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Because <a href="/wiki/Productivism" title="Productivism">productivism</a> was key to creating a strong nationalist state, it criticized internationalist and Marxist socialism, advocating instead to represent a type of nationalist productivist socialism. Nevertheless, while condemning parasitical capitalism, was willing to accommodate productivist capitalism within it so long as it supported the nationalist objective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpektorowskiIreni-Saban201333_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpektorowskiIreni-Saban201333-236">[236]</a></sup> The role of productivism was derived from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henri_de_Saint_Simon" title="Henri de Saint Simon">Henri de Saint Simon</a>, whose ideas inspired the creation of <a href="/wiki/Utopian_socialism" title="Utopian socialism">utopian socialism</a> and influenced other ideologies, that stressed solidarity rather than class war and whose conception of productive people in the economy included both productive workers and productive bosses to challenge the influence of the aristocracy and unproductive financial speculators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006535_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006535-237">[237]</a></sup> Saint Simon's vision combined the traditionalist right-wing criticisms of the French Revolution with a left-wing belief in the need for association or collaboration of productive people in society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006535_237-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006535-237">[237]</a></sup> Whereas Marxism condemned capitalism as a system of exploitative property relations, fascism saw the nature of the control of credit and money in the contemporary capitalist system as abusive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpektorowskiIreni-Saban201333_236-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpektorowskiIreni-Saban201333-236">[236]</a></sup> Unlike Marxism, fascism did not see class conflict between the Marxist-defined proletariat and the bourgeoisie as a given or as an engine of historical materialism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpektorowskiIreni-Saban201333_236-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpektorowskiIreni-Saban201333-236">[236]</a></sup> Instead, it viewed workers and productive capitalists in common as productive people who were in conflict with parasitic elements in society including: corrupt political parties, corrupt financial capital and feeble people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpektorowskiIreni-Saban201333_236-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpektorowskiIreni-Saban201333-236">[236]</a></sup> Fascist leaders such as Mussolini and Hitler spoke of the need to create a new managerial elite led by engineers and captains of industry—but free from the parasitic leadership of industries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpektorowskiIreni-Saban201333_236-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpektorowskiIreni-Saban201333-236">[236]</a></sup> Hitler stated that the Nazi Party supported <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">bodenständigen Kapitalismus</i></span> ("productive capitalism") that was based upon profit earned from one's own labour, but condemned unproductive capitalism or loan capitalism, which derived profit from speculation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman201124_238-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman201124-238">[238]</a></sup>
</p><p>Fascist economics supported a state-controlled economy that accepted a mix of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Private_ownership" title="Private ownership">private</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_ownership" title="Public ownership">public ownership</a> over the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMillward2007178_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMillward2007178-239">[239]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Economic_planning" title="Economic planning">Economic planning</a> was applied to both the public and private sector and the prosperity of private enterprise depended on its acceptance of synchronizing itself with the economic goals of the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006189_178-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006189-178">[178]</a></sup> Fascist economic ideology supported the <a href="/wiki/Profit_motive" title="Profit motive">profit motive</a>, but emphasized that industries must uphold the national interest as superior to private profit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006189_178-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006189-178">[178]</a></sup>
</p><p>While fascism accepted the importance of material wealth and power, it condemned materialism which identified as being present in both communism and <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalism</a> and criticized materialism for lacking acknowledgement of the role of the <a href="/wiki/Vitalism" title="Vitalism">spirit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaviesLynch2002103_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaviesLynch2002103-240">[240]</a></sup> In particular, fascists criticized capitalism, not because of its competitive nature nor support of private property, which fascists supported—but due to its materialism, individualism, alleged bourgeois decadence and alleged indifference to the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPaxton200510_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPaxton200510-241">[241]</a></sup> Fascism denounced Marxism for its advocacy of materialist internationalist class identity, which fascists regarded as an attack upon the emotional and spiritual bonds of the nation and a threat to the achievement of genuine national solidarity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBreuilly1994290_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBreuilly1994290-242">[242]</a></sup>
</p><p>In discussing the spread of fascism beyond Italy, historian Philip Morgan states: "Since the Depression was a crisis of laissez-faire capitalism and its political counterpart, parliamentary democracy, fascism could pose as the 'third-way' alternative between capitalism and Bolshevism, the model of a new European 'civilization.' As Mussolini typically put it in early 1934, 'from 1929 ... fascism has become a universal phenomenon ... The dominant forces of the 19th century, democracy, socialism, [and] liberalism have been exhausted ... the new political and economic forms of the twentieth-century are fascist' (Mussolini 1935: 32)."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorgan2003_168-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorgan2003-168">[168]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (October 2021)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Fascists criticized egalitarianism as preserving the weak, and they instead promoted social Darwinist views and policies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGriffinFeldman2004353_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGriffinFeldman2004353-243">[243]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHawkins1997285_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHawkins1997285-244">[244]</a></sup> They were in principle opposed to the idea of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_welfare" title="Social welfare">social welfare</a>, arguing that it "encouraged the preservation of the degenerate and the feeble."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005483–484_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005483–484-245">[245]</a></sup> The Nazi Party condemned the welfare system of the Weimar Republic, as well as private charity and philanthropy, for supporting people whom they regarded as racially inferior and weak, and who should have been weeded out in the process of natural selection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005484_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005484-246">[246]</a></sup> Nevertheless, faced with the mass unemployment and poverty of the Great Depression, the Nazis found it necessary to set up charitable institutions to help racially-pure Germans in order to maintain popular support, while arguing that this represented "racial self-help" and not indiscriminate charity or universal social welfare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005484–485_247-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005484–485-247">[247]</a></sup> Thus, Nazi programs such as the <a href="/wiki/Winterhilfswerk" title="Winterhilfswerk">Winter Relief of the German People</a> and the broader <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nationalsozialistische_Volkswohlfahrt" title="Nationalsozialistische Volkswohlfahrt">National Socialist People's Welfare</a> (NSV) were organized as quasi-private institutions, officially relying on private donations from Germans to help others of their race—although in practice those who refused to donate could face severe consequences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005486–487_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005486–487-248">[248]</a></sup> Unlike the social welfare institutions of the Weimar Republic and the Christian charities, the NSV distributed assistance on explicitly racial grounds. It provided support only to those who were "racially sound, capable of and willing to work, politically reliable, and willing and able to reproduce." Non-Aryans were excluded, as well as the "work-shy", "asocials" and the "hereditarily ill".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005489_249-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005489-249">[249]</a></sup> Under these conditions, by 1939, over 17 million Germans had obtained assistance from the NSV, and the agency "projected a powerful image of caring and support" for "those who were judged to have got into difficulties through no fault of their own."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005489_249-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005489-249">[249]</a></sup> Yet the organization was "feared and disliked among society's poorest" because it resorted to intrusive questioning and monitoring to judge who was worthy of support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005489–490_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005489–490-250">[250]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Action">Action</span></h3>
<p>Fascism emphasizes <a href="/wiki/Direct_action" title="Direct action">direct action</a>, including supporting the legitimacy of political violence, as a core part of its politics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPayne1995106Breuilly1994294_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPayne1995106Breuilly1994294-251">[251]</a></sup> Fascism views violent action as a necessity in politics that fascism identifies as being an "endless struggle";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWoodley2010106_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWoodley2010106-252">[252]</a></sup> this emphasis on the use of political violence means that most fascist parties have also created their own private <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Militias" title="Militias">militias</a> (e.g. the Nazi Party's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brown_shirts" title="Brown shirts">Brown shirts</a> and Fascist Italy's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milizia_Volontaria_per_la_Sicurezza_Nazionale" title="Milizia Volontaria per la Sicurezza Nazionale">Blackshirts</a>).
</p><p>The basis of fascism's support of violent action in politics is connected to social Darwinism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWoodley2010106_252-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWoodley2010106-252">[252]</a></sup> Fascist movements have commonly held social Darwinist views of nations, races and societies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPayne1995485–486_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPayne1995485–486-253">[253]</a></sup> They say that nations and races must purge themselves of socially and biologically weak or <a href="/wiki/Social_degeneration" title="Social degeneration">degenerate</a> people, while simultaneously promoting the creation of strong people, in order to survive in a world defined by perpetual national and racial conflict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGriffin199559_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGriffin199559-254">[254]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Age_and_gender_roles">Age and gender roles</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Piccole_Italiane.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2320" data-file-width="4020" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Piccole_Italiane.jpg/220px-Piccole_Italiane.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Piccole_Italiane.jpg/330px-Piccole_Italiane.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Piccole_Italiane.jpg/440px-Piccole_Italiane.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Piccole_Italiane.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Members of the <span title="Italian-language text"><i lang="it">Piccole Italiane</i></span>, an organization for girls within the National Fascist Party in Italy</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-04517A,_Potsdam,_M%C3%A4dchen_in_der_F%C3%BChrerinnenschule.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="542" data-file-width="797" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-04517A%2C_Potsdam%2C_M%C3%A4dchen_in_der_F%C3%BChrerinnenschule.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-04517A%2C_Potsdam%2C_M%C3%A4dchen_in_der_F%C3%BChrerinnenschule.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-04517A%2C_Potsdam%2C_M%C3%A4dchen_in_der_F%C3%BChrerinnenschule.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-04517A%2C_Potsdam%2C_M%C3%A4dchen_in_der_F%C3%BChrerinnenschule.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-04517A%2C_Potsdam%2C_M%C3%A4dchen_in_der_F%C3%BChrerinnenschule.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-04517A%2C_Potsdam%2C_M%C3%A4dchen_in_der_F%C3%BChrerinnenschule.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-04517A,_Potsdam,_M%C3%A4dchen_in_der_F%C3%BChrerinnenschule.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Members of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_German_Girls" title="League of German Girls">League of German Girls</a>, an organization for girls within the Nazi Party in Germany</div></div></div>
<p>Fascism emphasizes <a href="/wiki/Youth" title="Youth">youth</a> both in a physical sense of age and in a spiritual sense as related to virility and commitment to action.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAntliff2007171_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAntliff2007171-255">[255]</a></sup> The Italian Fascists' political anthem was called <i><a href="/wiki/Giovinezza" title="Giovinezza">Giovinezza</a></i> ("The Youth").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAntliff2007171_255-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAntliff2007171-255">[255]</a></sup> Fascism identifies the physical age period of youth as a critical time for the moral development of people who will affect society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuine199647_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuine199647-256">[256]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Walter_Laqueur" title="Walter Laqueur">Walter Laqueur</a> argues that "[t]he corollaries of the cult of war and physical danger were the cult of brutality, strength, and sexuality ... [fascism is] a true counter-civilization: rejecting the sophisticated rationalist humanism of Old Europe, fascism sets up as its ideal the primitive instincts and primal emotions of the barbarian."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaqueur1978341_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaqueur1978341-257">[257]</a></sup>
</p><p>Italian Fascism pursued what it called "moral hygiene" of youth, particularly regarding <a href="/wiki/Human_sexuality" title="Human sexuality">sexuality</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuine199646–47_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuine199646–47-258">[258]</a></sup> Fascist Italy promoted what it considered normal sexual behaviour in youth while denouncing what it considered deviant sexual behaviour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuine199646–47_258-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuine199646–47-258">[258]</a></sup> It condemned <a href="/wiki/Pornography" title="Pornography">pornography</a>, most forms of <a href="/wiki/Birth_control" title="Birth control">birth control</a> and contraceptive devices (with the exception of the <a href="/wiki/Condom" title="Condom">condom</a>), <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prostitution" title="Prostitution">prostitution</a> as deviant sexual behaviour, although enforcement of laws opposed to such practices was erratic and authorities often turned a blind eye.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuine199646–47_258-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuine199646–47-258">[258]</a></sup> Fascist Italy regarded the promotion of male sexual excitation before <a href="/wiki/Puberty" title="Puberty">puberty</a> as the cause of criminality amongst male youth, declared homosexuality a social disease and pursued an aggressive campaign to reduce prostitution of young women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuine199646–47_258-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuine199646–47-258">[258]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mussolini perceived women's primary role as primarily child bearers, while that of men as warriors, once saying: "War is to man what maternity is to the woman."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBollas1993205_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBollas1993205-259">[259]</a></sup> In an effort to increase birthrates, the Italian Fascist government gave financial incentives to women who raised large families and initiated policies intended to reduce the number of women employed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcDonald199927_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDonald199927-260">[260]</a></sup> Italian Fascism called for women to be honoured as "reproducers of the nation" and the Italian Fascist government held ritual ceremonies to honour women's role within the Italian nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMann2004101_261-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMann2004101-261">[261]</a></sup> In 1934, Mussolini declared that employment of women was a "major aspect of the thorny problem of unemployment" and that for women, working was "incompatible with childbearing"; Mussolini went on to say that the solution to unemployment for men was the "exodus of women from the work force."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDurham199815_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDurham199815-262">[262]</a></sup>
</p><p>The German Nazi government strongly encouraged women to stay at home to bear children and keep house.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005331–332_263-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005331–332-263">[263]</a></sup> This policy was reinforced by bestowing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cross_of_Honor_of_the_German_Mother" title="Cross of Honor of the German Mother">Cross of Honor of the German Mother</a> on women bearing four or more children. The unemployment rate was cut substantially, mostly through arms production and sending women home so that men could take their jobs. Nazi propaganda sometimes promoted premarital and extramarital sexual relations, unwed motherhood and divorce, but at other times the Nazis opposed such behaviour.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The Nazis decriminalized abortion in cases where fetuses had hereditary defects or were of a race the government disapproved of, while the abortion of healthy pure German, <a href="/wiki/Aryan_race" title="Aryan race">Aryan</a> fetuses remained strictly forbidden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedlander1995[httpsbooksgooglecomidgqLDEKVk2nMCprintsecfrontcover_30]_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedlander1995[httpsbooksgooglecomidgqLDEKVk2nMCprintsecfrontcover_30]-264">[264]</a></sup> For non-Aryans, abortion was often compulsory. Their <a href="/wiki/Eugenics" title="Eugenics">eugenics</a> program also stemmed from the "progressive biomedical model" of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weimar_Germany" title="Weimar Germany">Weimar Germany</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLaren1999139_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLaren1999139-265">[265]</a></sup> In 1935, Nazi Germany expanded the legality of <a href="/wiki/History_of_abortion" title="History of abortion">abortion</a> by amending <a href="/wiki/Law_for_the_Prevention_of_Hereditarily_Diseased_Offspring" title="Law for the Prevention of Hereditarily Diseased Offspring">its eugenics law</a>, to promote abortion for women with hereditary disorders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedlander1995[httpsbooksgooglecomidgqLDEKVk2nMCprintsecfrontcover_30]_264-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedlander1995[httpsbooksgooglecomidgqLDEKVk2nMCprintsecfrontcover_30]-264">[264]</a></sup> The law allowed abortion if a woman gave her permission and the fetus was not yet viable<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEProctor1989366_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEProctor1989366-266">[266]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArnotUsborne1999[httpsbooksgooglecomidq1BFiRa3KHkCprintsecfrontcover_241]_267-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArnotUsborne1999[httpsbooksgooglecomidq1BFiRa3KHkCprintsecfrontcover_241]-267">[267]</a></sup> and for purposes of so-called <a href="/wiki/Racial_hygiene" title="Racial hygiene">racial hygiene</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEProctor1989122–123_268-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEProctor1989122–123-268">[268]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETierney1999[httpsbooksgooglecomidgQLqRd7hJq0Cprintsecfrontcover_589]_269-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETierney1999[httpsbooksgooglecomidgQLqRd7hJq0Cprintsecfrontcover_589]-269">[269]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Nazis said that homosexuality was degenerate, effeminate, perverted and undermined masculinity because it did not produce children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2005529_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2005529-270">[270]</a></sup> They considered homosexuality curable through therapy, citing modern <a href="/wiki/Scientism" title="Scientism">scientism</a> and the study of <a href="/wiki/Sexology" title="Sexology">sexology</a>, which said that homosexuality could be felt by "normal" people and not just an abnormal minority.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Open homosexuals were interned in Nazi concentration camps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Palingenesis_and_modernism">Palingenesis and modernism</span></h3>
<p>Fascism emphasizes both palingenesis (national rebirth or re-creation) and <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">modernism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006168_272-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006168-272">[272]</a></sup> In particular, fascism's nationalism has been identified as having a palingenetic character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006451–453_273-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006451–453-273">[273]</a></sup> Fascism promotes the regeneration of the nation and purging it of decadence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006168_272-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006168-272">[272]</a></sup> Fascism accepts forms of modernism that it deems promotes national regeneration while rejecting forms of modernism that are regarded as antithetical to national regeneration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006168–169_274-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlamires2006168–169-274">[274]</a></sup> Fascism aestheticized modern technology and its association with speed, power and violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeocleous199763_275-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeocleous199763-275">[275]</a></sup> Fascism admired advances in the economy in the early 20th century, particularly <a href="/wiki/Fordism" title="Fordism">Fordism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scientific_management" title="Scientific management">scientific management</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeocleous199765_276-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeocleous199765-276">[276]</a></sup> Fascist modernism has been recognized as inspired or developed by various figures—such as Filippo Tommaso Marinetti, <a href="/wiki/Ernst_J%C3%BCnger" title="Ernst Jünger">Ernst Jünger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gottfried_Benn" title="Gottfried Benn">Gottfried Benn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louis-Ferdinand_C%C3%A9line" title="Louis-Ferdinand Céline">Louis-Ferdinand Céline</a>, <a href="/wiki/Knut_Hamsun" title="Knut Hamsun">Knut Hamsun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ezra_Pound" title="Ezra Pound">Ezra Pound</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wyndham_Lewis" title="Wyndham Lewis">Wyndham Lewis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWelge2007547_277-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWelge2007547-277">[277]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Italy, such modernist influence was exemplified by Marinetti who advocated a palingenetic modernist society that condemned liberal-bourgeois values of tradition and psychology, while promoting a technological-martial religion of national renewal that emphasized militant nationalism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWelge2007550_278-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWelge2007550-278">[278]</a></sup> In Germany, it was exemplified by Jünger who was influenced by his observation of the technological warfare during World War I and claimed that a new social class had been created that he described as the "warrior-worker";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWelge2007553_279-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWelge2007553-279">[279]</a></sup> Like Marinetti, Jünger emphasized the revolutionary capacities of technology. He emphasized an "organic construction" between human and machine as a liberating and regenerative force that challenged liberal democracy, conceptions of individual autonomy, bourgeois nihilism and decadence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWelge2007553_279-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWelge2007553-279">[279]</a></sup> He conceived of a society based on a totalitarian concept of "total mobilization" of such disciplined warrior-workers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWelge2007553_279-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWelge2007553-279">[279]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fascist_aesthetics">Fascist aesthetics</span></h3>
<p>According to cultural critic <a href="/wiki/Susan_Sontag" title="Susan Sontag">Susan Sontag</a>, "[f]ascist aesthetics ... flow from (and justify) a preoccupation with situations of control, submissive behavior, extravagant effort, and the endurance of pain; they endorse two seemingly opposite states, egomania and servitude. The relations of domination and enslavement take the form of a characteristic pageantry: the massing of groups of people; the turning of people into things; the multiplication or replication of things; and the grouping of people/things around an all-powerful, hypnotic leader-figure or force. The fascist dramaturgy centers on the orgiastic transactions between mighty forces and their puppets, uniformly garbed and shown in ever swelling numbers. Its choreography alternates between ceaseless motion and a congealed, static, 'virile' posing. Fascist art glorifies surrender, it exalts mindlessness, it glamorizes death."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESontag1975_280-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESontag1975-280">[280]</a></sup> Sontag also enumerates some commonalities between fascist art and the official art of communist countries, such as the obeisance of the masses to the hero, and a preference for the monumental and the "grandiose and rigid" choreography of mass bodies. But whereas official communist art "aims to expound and reinforce a utopian morality", the art of fascist countries such as Nazi Germany "displays a utopian aesthetics – that of physical perfection", in a way that is "both prurient and idealizing".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESontag1975_280-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESontag1975-280">[280]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to Sontag, fascist aesthetics "is based on the containment of vital forces; movements are confined, held tight, held in." Its appeal is not necessarily limited to those who share the fascist political ideology because fascism "stands for an ideal or rather ideals that are persistent today under the other banners: the ideal of life as art, the cult of beauty, the fetishism of courage, the dissolution of alienation in ecstatic feelings of community; the repudiation of the intellect; the family of man (under the parenthood of leaders)."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESontag1975_280-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESontag1975-280">[280]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span></h2>
<p>Fascism has been widely criticized and condemned in modern times since the defeat of the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a> in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anti-democratic_and_tyrannical">Anti-democratic and tyrannical</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_democracy" title="Criticism of democracy">Criticism of democracy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hitler_and_Franco_at_Hendaye_(en.wiki).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3500" data-file-width="2430" decoding="async" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Hitler_and_Franco_at_Hendaye_%28en.wiki%29.jpg/170px-Hitler_and_Franco_at_Hendaye_%28en.wiki%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Hitler_and_Franco_at_Hendaye_%28en.wiki%29.jpg/255px-Hitler_and_Franco_at_Hendaye_%28en.wiki%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Hitler_and_Franco_at_Hendaye_%28en.wiki%29.jpg/340px-Hitler_and_Franco_at_Hendaye_%28en.wiki%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hitler_and_Franco_at_Hendaye_(en.wiki).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hitler and Spanish dictator <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a> in <a href="/wiki/Meeting_at_Hendaye" title="Meeting at Hendaye">Meeting at Hendaye</a>, on 23 October 1940</div></div></div>
<p>One of the most common and strongest criticisms of fascism is that it is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tyranny" title="Tyranny">tyranny</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoesche201011_281-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoesche201011-281">[281]</a></sup> Fascism is deliberately and entirely non-democratic and anti-democratic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClarkeFoweraker2001540Pollard1998121Griffin199142_282-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClarkeFoweraker2001540Pollard1998121Griffin199142-282">[282]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unprincipled_opportunism">Unprincipled opportunism</span></h3>
<p>Some critics of Italian fascism have said that much of the ideology was merely a by-product of unprincipled <a href="/wiki/Opportunism" title="Opportunism">opportunism</a> by Mussolini and that he changed his political stances merely to bolster his personal ambitions while he disguised them as being purposeful to the public.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchreiberStegemannVogel1995111_283-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchreiberStegemannVogel1995111-283">[283]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Washburn_Child" title="Richard Washburn Child">Richard Washburn Child</a>, the American ambassador to Italy who worked with Mussolini and became his friend and admirer, defended Mussolini's opportunistic behaviour by writing: "Opportunist is a term of reproach used to brand men who fit themselves to conditions for the reasons of self-interest. Mussolini, as I have learned to know him, is an opportunist in the sense that he believed that mankind itself must be fitted to changing conditions rather than to fixed theories, no matter how many hopes and prayers have been expended on theories and programmes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup> Child quoted Mussolini as saying: "The sanctity of an ism is not in the ism; it has no sanctity beyond its power to do, to work, to succeed in practice. It may have succeeded yesterday and fail to-morrow. Failed yesterday and succeed to-morrow. The machine, first of all, must run!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMussolini1998ix_285-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMussolini1998ix-285">[285]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some have criticized Mussolini's actions during the outbreak of World War I as opportunistic for seeming to suddenly abandon Marxist egalitarian internationalism for non-egalitarian <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a> and note, to that effect, that upon Mussolini endorsing Italy's intervention in the war against Germany and Austria-Hungary, he and the new fascist movement received financial support from Italian and foreign sources, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Ansaldo_company" title="Italian Ansaldo company">Ansaldo</a> (an armaments firm) and other companies<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMack_Smith1997284_286-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMack_Smith1997284-286">[286]</a></sup> as well as the British Security Service <a href="/wiki/MI5" title="MI5">MI5</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian2009-10-13_287-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian2009-10-13-287">[287]</a></sup> Some, including Mussolini's socialist opponents at the time, have noted that regardless of the financial support he accepted for his pro-interventionist stance, Mussolini was free to write whatever he wished in his newspaper <span title="Italian-language text"><i lang="it">Il Popolo d'Italia</i></span> without prior sanctioning from his financial backers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEO'Brien201437_288-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Brien201437-288">[288]</a></sup> Furthermore, the major source of financial support that Mussolini and the fascist movement received in World War I was from France and is widely believed to have been French socialists who supported the French government's war against Germany and who sent support to Italian socialists who wanted Italian intervention on France's side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGregor1979200_289-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGregor1979200-289">[289]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mussolini's transformation away from Marxism into what eventually became fascism began prior to World War I, as Mussolini had grown increasingly pessimistic about Marxism and egalitarianism while becoming increasingly supportive of figures who opposed egalitarianism, such as Friedrich Nietzsche.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGolombWistrich2002249_290-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGolombWistrich2002249-290">[290]</a></sup> By 1902, Mussolini was studying Georges Sorel, Nietzsche and <a href="/wiki/Vilfredo_Pareto" title="Vilfredo Pareto">Vilfredo Pareto</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDelzel197096_291-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDelzel197096-291">[291]</a></sup> Sorel's emphasis on the need for overthrowing decadent liberal democracy and capitalism by the use of violence, direct action, general strikes and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Machiavelli" title="Machiavelli">neo-Machiavellian</a> appeals to emotion impressed Mussolini deeply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDelzel19703_292-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDelzel19703-292">[292]</a></sup> Mussolini's use of Nietzsche made him a highly unorthodox socialist, due to Nietzsche's promotion of elitism and anti-egalitarian views.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGolombWistrich2002249_290-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGolombWistrich2002249-290">[290]</a></sup> Prior to World War I, Mussolini's writings over time indicated that he had abandoned the Marxism and egalitarianism that he had previously supported in favour of Nietzsche's <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de">übermensch</i></span> concept and anti-egalitarianism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGolombWistrich2002249_290-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGolombWistrich2002249-290">[290]</a></sup> In 1908, Mussolini wrote a short essay called "Philosophy of Strength" based on his Nietzschean influence, in which Mussolini openly spoke fondly of the ramifications of an impending war in Europe in challenging both religion and <a href="/wiki/Nihilism" title="Nihilism">nihilism</a>: "[A] new kind of free spirit will come, strengthened by the war, ... a spirit equipped with a kind of sublime perversity, ... a new free spirit will triumph over God and over Nothing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGori200414_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGori200414-113">[113]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ideological_dishonesty">Ideological dishonesty</span></h3>
<p>Fascism has been criticized for being ideologically dishonest. Major examples of ideological dishonesty have been identified in Italian fascism's changing relationship with German Nazism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGillette200117Pollard1998129_293-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGillette200117Pollard1998129-293">[293]</a></sup> Fascist Italy's official foreign policy positions were known to commonly utilize rhetorical ideological <a href="/wiki/Hyperbole" title="Hyperbole">hyperbole</a> to justify its actions, although during <a href="/wiki/Dino_Grandi" title="Dino Grandi">Dino Grandi</a>'s tenure as Italy's foreign minister the country engaged in <span title="German-language text"><i lang="de"><a href="/wiki/Realpolitik" title="Realpolitik">realpolitik</a></i></span> free of such fascist hyperbole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurgwyn199758_294-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurgwyn199758-294">[294]</a></sup> Italian fascism's stance towards German Nazism fluctuated from support from the late 1920s to 1934, when it celebrated Hitler's rise to power and Mussolini's first meeting with Hitler in 1934; to opposition from 1934 to 1936 after the assassination of Italy's allied leader in Austria, <a href="/wiki/Engelbert_Dollfuss" title="Engelbert Dollfuss">Engelbert Dollfuss</a>, by Austrian Nazis; and again back to support after 1936, when Germany was the only significant power that did not denounce <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italy%27s_invasion_and_occupation_of_Ethiopia" title="Italy's invasion and occupation of Ethiopia">Italy's invasion and occupation of Ethiopia</a>.
</p><p>After antagonism exploded between Nazi Germany and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Fascist Italy</a> over the assassination of Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss in 1934, Mussolini and Italian fascists denounced and ridiculed Nazism's racial theories, particularly by denouncing its <a href="/wiki/Nordic_race" title="Nordic race">Nordicism</a>, while promoting <a href="/wiki/Mediterraneanism" title="Mediterraneanism">Mediterraneanism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPollard1998129_295-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPollard1998129-295">[295]</a></sup> Mussolini himself responded to Nordicists' claims of Italy being divided into Nordic and Mediterranean racial areas due to Germanic invasions of Northern Italy by claiming that while Germanic tribes such as the <a href="/wiki/Lombards" title="Lombards">Lombards</a> took control of Italy after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fall_of_Ancient_Rome" title="Fall of Ancient Rome">fall of Ancient Rome</a>, they arrived in small numbers (about 8,000) and quickly assimilated into Roman culture and spoke the <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Latin</a> language within fifty years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGillette200193_296-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGillette200193-296">[296]</a></sup> Italian fascism was influenced by the tradition of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_nationalists" title="Italian nationalists">Italian nationalists</a> scornfully looking down upon Nordicists' claims and taking pride in comparing the age and sophistication of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Roman_civilization" title="Ancient Roman civilization">ancient Roman civilization</a> as well as the classical revival in the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> to that of Nordic societies that Italian nationalists described as "newcomers" to civilization in comparison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGillette200117_297-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGillette200117-297">[297]</a></sup> At the height of antagonism between the Nazis and Italian fascists over race, Mussolini claimed that the Germans themselves were not a pure race and noted with irony that the Nazi theory of German racial superiority was based on the theories of non-German foreigners, such as Frenchman Arthur de Gobineau.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGillette200145_298-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGillette200145-298">[298]</a></sup> After the tension in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German-Italian_relations" title="German-Italian relations">German-Italian relations</a> diminished during the late 1930s, Italian fascism sought to harmonize its ideology with German Nazism and combined Nordicist and Mediterranean racial theories, noting that Italians were members of the Aryan Race, composed of a mixed Nordic-Mediterranean subtype.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPollard1998129_295-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPollard1998129-295">[295]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1938, Mussolini declared upon Italy's adoption of antisemitic laws that Italian fascism had always been antisemitic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPollard1998129_295-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPollard1998129-295">[295]</a></sup> In fact, Italian fascism did not endorse <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">antisemitism</a> until the late 1930s when Mussolini feared alienating antisemitic Nazi Germany, whose power and influence were growing in Europe. Prior to that period, there had been notable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_Italians" title="Jewish Italians">Jewish Italians</a> who had been senior Italian fascist officials, including <a href="/wiki/Margherita_Sarfatti" title="Margherita Sarfatti">Margherita Sarfatti</a>, who had also been Mussolini's mistress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPollard1998129_295-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPollard1998129-295">[295]</a></sup> Also contrary to Mussolini's claim in 1938, only a small number of Italian fascists were staunchly antisemitic (such as <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Farinacci" title="Roberto Farinacci">Roberto Farinacci</a> and Giuseppe Preziosi), while others such as <a href="/wiki/Italo_Balbo" title="Italo Balbo">Italo Balbo</a>, who came from <a href="/wiki/Ferrara" title="Ferrara">Ferrara</a> which had one of Italy's largest Jewish communities, were disgusted by the antisemitic laws and opposed them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPollard1998129_295-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPollard1998129-295">[295]</a></sup> Fascism scholar Mark Neocleous notes that while Italian fascism did not have a clear commitment to antisemitism, there were occasional antisemitic statements issued prior to 1938, such as Mussolini in 1919 declaring that the Jewish bankers in London and New York were connected by race to the Russian Bolsheviks and that eight percent of the Russian Bolsheviks were Jews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeocleous199735–36_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeocleous199735–36-299">[299]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFBerend2016"><a href="/wiki/Iv%C3%A1n_T._Berend" title="Iván T. <li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFLynchDavies2002">Lynch, Derek; Davies, Peter J. (2002). <i>The Routledge Companion to Fascism and the Far Right</i>. United Kingdom: <a href="/wiki/Routledge" title="Routledge">Routledge</a>. p. 275. <q>Detailed and intrusive state direction of the economy and/or society. Dirigisme was central to both fascism and Communist systems. </li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEMuddeKaltwasser20176,_33–34-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMuddeKaltwasser20176,_33–34_49-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMuddeKaltwasser2017">Mudde &amp; Kaltwasser (2017)</a>, pp. 6, 33–34: "... thin-centered ideologies have a restricted morphology, which necessarily appears attached to—and sometimes is even assimilated into—other ideologies. In fact, populism almost always appears attached to other ideological elements, which are crucial for the promotion of political projects that are appealing to a broader public. Consequently, by itself populism can offer neither complex nor comprehensive answers to the political questions that modern societies generate. ... [Populism] is not so much a coherent ideological tradition as a set of ideas that, in the real world, appears in combination with quite different, and sometimes contradictory, ideologies." (p.6)</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEGriffinFeldman2004353-243"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGriffinFeldman2004353_243-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFGriffinFeldman2004">Griffin &amp; Feldman (2004)</a>, p. 353: "When the Russian revolution occurred in 1917 and the 'Democratic' revolution spread after the First World War, anti-<a href="/wiki/Bolshevism" title="Bolshevism">bolshevism</a> and anti-egalitarianism rose as very strong "restoration movements" on the European scene. However, by the turn of that century no one could predict that fascism would become such a concrete, political reaction ... ."</span>

<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEHawkins1997285-244"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHawkins1997285_244-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFHawkins1997">Hawkins (1997)</a>, p. 285: "Conflict is in fact the basic law of life in all social organisms, as it is of all biological ones; societies are formed, gain strength, and move forwards through conflict; the healthiest and most vital of them assert themselves against the weakest and less well adapted through conflict; the natural evolution of nations and races takes place through conflict." Alfredo Rocco, Italian Fascist.</span>

On 10 November 1938, a Luneberg court declared abortion legal for Jews."</span>

<li><a class="external text" href="http://media.wix.com/ugd/927b40_c1ee26114a4d480cb048f5f96a4cc68f.pdf" rel="nofollow">Authorized translation of Mussolini's "The Political and Social Doctrine of Fascism" (1933)</a> (PDF). media.wix.com.</li>
<li><a class="extiw" href="https://www.gutenberg.org/ebooks/14058" title="gutenberg:14058">Readings on Fascism and National Socialism by Various – Project Gutenberg</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130930081524/http://www.themodernword.com/eco/eco_blackshirt.html" rel="nofollow">"Eternal Fascism: Fourteen Ways of Looking at a Blackshirt"</a> – <a href="/wiki/Umberto_Eco" title="Umberto Eco">Umberto Eco</a>'s list of 14 characteristics of Fascism, originally published 1995.</li></ul>
